<text>Best storage rental experience ever. Laura is super friendly and helpful.

Update: the customer service here is fine, no complaints. However, if you're considering public storage vs another company, there are some things to consider.

1. This location has never, in the months ive been renting here, had carts or flatbeds available for tenant use, as other companies do.
2. Public storage does not allow prorated rent when moving out, as other companies do.
3. Public storage does not allow combination locks, supposedly because they are not secure. I used a combination lock for years at another facility, with no issues. < review>
i moved to this location from another public storage facility just a mile down the road. what a difference! when my girlfriend and i got into the new unit, we literally both sighed. the clerk (karen) that checked me in was courteous and informative. the other tenants are polite and considerate.

i met the manager the next day after moving in, while she was making her rounds. i would describe her (joyce) as assertive, easy going, and informative. she answered all my questions about her place, and cleared up a possible dispute i was considering against the previous facility due to unclear information about my move out date. she literally saved me time and money. i've got everything i paid for.

the bathroom has never been dirty (we use it a lot, we have 5yr old twins), or out of order. the kids enjoy going there to sort things, organize photos, etc., i feel safe bringing them there, and that's a big relief.

i could not say these things about the previous public storage facility just down the road, which we will forever call "zombieland", because of the obvious drug user types, the out of order bathroom (my boys and i had to hide in our unit, and pee in bottles), and the inattentive staff.

i attribute all these differences to the staff. joyce rocks! karen rocks! erica rocks! and everyone else there i may not have met yet, you guys rock. i will recomend the place, and when necessary, we will be back.

btw- this is my first testimonial ever and it feels great, thanks!

<review>Heartsleeves uses beans from Swell, a small coffee roaster over in Point Loma. Espresso tastes up to snuff and has slight caramel tones with a bitter finish. It seems to be a lighter roast but acidity is well balanced.
The uniqueness of this tiny shop is the specialty drinks which they've named with interesting names such as Be Loved and Dutchess, which incorporate cinnamon, cardamom and other spices not traditional here in the US, for which I salute them.
Eclectic interior and wise use of the small space give it a welcoming, friendly feel. It may be a good idea for clients to be able to smell some of those spicy ingredients in anticipation of their beverage. Just putting it out there :)</review><Rating>4<//Rating><Date>1473554248897< /Date>< Response>

<Rate>4< /Rate>< review>
*Open for take-out and delivery, also on Grubhub and DoorDash Sept 2020* Servers were wearing masks, but I didn't see any gloves on the cashier.

Dishes I recommend include Chicken or lamb Biryani, Lamb Vindaloo, Okra, Butter Chicken (that sauce), and mixed platter appetizer.

Tips:
1) You can get a $5 off certificate for $2 at restaurant.com (must spend $15 or more)
2) Every dish is $1 more expensive on Doordash than on the menu</review>

< review>
Oh my goodness where do I begin. I am from Sacramento CA and found myself in the town of Tracy. I came across this place on Yelp and after seeing the great reviews I had to try this place.
I walked inside and was welcomed by no one and a dark room, I thought the place was closed but then a lady appeared and greeted me. She took my order (not the best customer service but it's alright I'm taking this to go) and told me it would be a 25-30 min wait. I ordered the veggie samosas, mixed pakora, two orders of tikki masala extra spicy, and a order of butter chicken and the best part is it only came out to $51!!! Feeding a family for $50 is a win in my books! The food was all amazing, this by far is the best tikki masala I have ever had!< /review>

<rating>4<//rating><Text>Dhaba Indian Cuisine has been in Tracy for awhile, and it has been a great addition to the ever growing food scene.  My friends and family come here often whenever we're craving delicious Indian food.

My family and I always get garlic naan, tandoori chicken, and mango lassi.  We switch up the curries now and then, but the chana masala and mango chicken are my favorites.  My parents have been getting the veggie biryani rice, on top of ordering white rice.  The biryani goes well with the tandoori chicken, while I find the white rice doesn't compete with the curries.

The restaurant looks small, but it can accommodate, I would say, two parties of 8 at the same time.  I haven't been to there for lunch, where they offer the food buffet style.  I'd like to do so soon.  I wish Dhaba continued success!<//Text>< Pics>

<review>Another reason to visit Paso Robles. We came for a wine country weekend and Sensorio for something to do in the evening. Only a couple of miles up 46 past 101.

They do do a temp check (as of 4-24-21) a bag check and there and you are responsible for social-distancing yourself on the walk. People can kind of crowd so it up to you to make space - and its dark.

Best time to come is just before sundown so you can get the contrast of the night sky above, dusk on the horizon and the lights.

We paid extra for the VIP but I don't think it was worth it personally. You have a place to sit above the walk and one free drink but the night we came it was soooo damn cold and the wind blowing we couldn't enjoy it.< /review>< pics>

We had a nice night. Arrived before sunset, grabbed an 805 beer & some food at the food truck court before enjoying a friday evening stroll around the grounds. I do think that eventually, post Covid-19, the light towers would be an awesome area ro add synchronized music & dancing; maybe as part of the VIP passes. As a photographer ot would be cool to have this used as a midnight astrophotography workshop venue where someone could pay a fair amount of money to receive professional instruction & use a tripod. The possibilities for this venue are endless so if you've already been I think they will be able to continue to entice return engagement of new exhibits & changes. Maybe even future concert grounds. Who knows, but as a local I did find this a nice evening for local & tourists alike . . .</text>

< Review>
We got the VIP tix and they were well worth it. We went when they opened (in order to watch the transformation from light to sunset) and we bypassed the already very very long line and were escorted to a roped off area with heaters, fireplaces and tables and chairs and an airstream ‚Äúbar‚Äù where one could order beer wine and champagne. Very nice experience. We had our wine and then decided to walk the path of which there are two. The longer path is not at all long so o would recommend that path. It‚Äôs a very easy walk. There are about 5-6 food trucks and various benches around the area. But seating is limited for the non-VIP ticket holders FYI<//Review>

<name>Kimberly Ann Graham</name>< Date>
1568298507301< /Date>
<rating>5< /rating>< Text>
Breathtaking! I highly recommend coming out while this installation is here. I also would recommend that you get a time slot that starts before the sun sets so that you can enjoy seeing the field during the process of the sun coming down and the lights coming up! There is plenty of parking and they limit entries to 75 people part time slot. I imagine it could get crowded but it certainly wasn't on my visit. As for accessibility, this has been designed with that in mind. All of the trails are 100% wheelchair accessible. They also have a large golf cart shuttle that will bring you from the parking area to the start of the trail around the field.  for food, the menu is a bit pedestrian so I can't recommend getting food here but the wine list is far better than average. The Opollo Zinfandel was delightful and served in a plastic stemless glass so it could be taken out on the trail.  No selfie sticks or tripods allowed but photography is welcome as long as it is personal photos & video.  they have blankets to rent for $5 if you fail to dress properly for the evening. They also have games on the lawn and a picnic area for food purchased on site. No outside food or beverages allowed.< /Text>

<review>The light display is lovely.  We really enjoyed photographing the colorful hillsides as we meandered through the lights. We selected the second hour so we could have dinner beforehand.  There may be photo ops at the first hour when the sky is not quite as dark.  Our disappointment was that the one-way path is not clearly marked. There are arrows on the ground which are difficult or impossible to see and little to no signage or human direction, except when you have already gone the wrong way.  There were also dark areas where the lights were out.  Don't recommend until these issues are fixed.<//review>< response>

<gmap_id>0x80ecc5443242f2c1:0xbf8e837bf16cd744<//gmap_id><response>None<//response><rating>4</rating><review>Unique experience that's literally a field of lights. We arrived before sundown to see what the installation looked like before dark. You can choose the VIP experience which included a boxed dinner, two drinks, and a reserved seating patio or join the commoners like us grabbing a glass of wine and some tacos from Ricky‚Äôs Mexican food truck permanently parked on site. We walked through the paths woven between a few large Oaks to view the open areas filled with small spheres that would soon be illuminated by fiber-optic light, gently swaying on their long stems. Very cool as the dusk turns to night, the moon hangs overhead filtering between the outstretched Oak branches while the thousands of small spheres gently change color. Not something we thought would be captivating but certainly was a sight to see. The installation is currently scheduled to run until January 2020, followed by grand plans for a new Hotel, Resort, and Botanical garden.<//review><time>1573096857044</time><username>Bondiamo< /username><UserId.>104283237201242085973< /UserId.></record>

< review>
Such an amazing experience! $30 (if you pay online), $34 + change (if you buy tickets from the gate). The employees are great, the bathroom is clean and modern, and nice music. As you pass the "activity center", you'll see the field of lights. The walk path is a little bit too dark (hope they add some very dim lights). I was awe by how majestic this place is! You can't do flash photography unfortunately, and you cannot use tripod too (you gotta be creative for manual exposure) . If you are planning to go take a photo of yourself with the background, use another phone and turn up its brightness and get a white background so you can use it as your mini spotlight!! Overall, I'm really happy with the experience that I have. It does feel like I'm on a magical place. I do hope someday this place gets improved over time. If Holidays are coming, I hope they put lights on the trees as well. Put more lights around the  area (even in the parking lot). I also hope they add more grass area there (fake or not). I would suggest you to wear shoes as the trail is sandy.  Overall, I HIGHLY RECOMMEND THIS PLACE!

Update: I highly recommend you use a phone with night mode- such as Galaxy S10, Note 10 and iPhone 11 Pro<//review>

<review>It is something you should try to see at least once. One thing was that the pizza booth worker was flustered or just off but he got our order wrong then didn't want us to pay until we were going to leave, we tried multiple times & we'd get sent away. At first it wasn't a big deal we assumed he didn't want to get his hands dirty cause he was in the middle of making multiple pizzas. Then we go a third time & he stares blankly, we asked if he took card before ordering & we reminded him of this, but he didn't have his phone or card reader it was a bit odd. Anyways ! The tickets do run quite high especially cause there is not too many food options or alcohol, so that is why this will be a one time thing. The art is solar powered & the lights don't turn on until the sun is down, so if you do get the 7pm ticket you may have to wait until 8pm or so to actually see them lit up. But it is absolutely amazing to get there early & see how everything looks before the lights come on & then as each one slowly comes on. It is breathtaking & at some time you should put your phone down & just enjoy the view.</review></record></dataset><record>

<rate>1<//rate><text>This is an...interesting experience. This is a set of 50k+ fiber optic cables that are fed into frosted plastic bulbs roughly 2" in diameter,  that look like the dandelions ready to seed that you blow. They are spread across a small valley and very (very) slowly change colors. No music, just walk through them. To give one credit, it's peaceful. Everyone was uniformly looking for spots as if something was going to happen...nope.

On the other hand, for the price it's expensive unless if you REALLY care about your Instagram. It's a 20 minute walk through high tech Christmas lights in a field for almost $40. This is a $20 experience, tops.

If this wasn't enough, we bought tickets for 8:30 pm, our tickets said that "your wave starts at 8". We show up at 8 and then are told they don't even start processing the line until 8:30. It's 9 and we finally made it in.

Supposedly it's between this and a botanical garden. City officials: pick the botanical garden.</text>< pics>

< Text>
I loved it! Its worth the $$ and drive if you're coming from a distance. We went within the first couple weeks of opening so things may change as time goes on.
-Waze had us turn into the wrong street which had us making a few u-turns on the freeway to get to the entrance.
-We chose the first time slot so we had plenty of time to eat and enjoy the live music before the sunset. You'll be fine with any time slot you choose.
-Dont be afraid to wander thru the exhibit before the sun goes down. It'll be beautiful from anywhere you stand.
-You'll want to stay until closing so plan on staying in town for the night or prepare for a late drive home.
-The food available from the food truck is pretty tasty. The portions are enough to get you by but if you're looking to have a full meal, eat before.
-Bring a sweater, wear comfy shoes, leave the hydroflask in the car.
-I'm sure the VIP section is great, but there's nothing like hanging around with the commoners.
-The bathroom portable was clean and well stocked.
-I will most definitely be returning.</Text>

< Time>

<Rate>4< /Rate><Review>Sensorio is currently exhibiting Bruno Munro‚Äôs Field of Lights which is a solar powered art installation that spread through multiple acres of land. The field is lit by sphere pods connecting to fiber-optics. They change colors every few seconds. It‚Äôs a beautiful experience and photo op! Tickets are purchased online with designated time and date.

Entrance/Parking: The entrance is located on one side of the freeway so you might be routed to loop around. There is a right turn lane from the freeway that leads directly to the parking lot. They offer complementary parking and shuttle service. A 5 minute walk to the entrance.

I came during Memorial weekend and they‚Äôve been open for about a week now. It looks like they are not completely done with the construction for the event such as fence, pavement, and lights for the entrance but the art installation is ready to view.

At the entrance, I was told we couldn‚Äôt bring in any camera with detachable lenses because they consider those professional cameras... I wasn‚Äôt gonna let that go since we drove all the way and obviously want to take photos. So I went to talk to a few staff members and sadly they didn‚Äôt even know the difference between a prof. camera.... Luckily, the executive director was right next to me and she was able to clear the misunderstanding to her staff. CAMERAS ARE ALLOWED but no tripods, professional camera crews, & photos for commercial use. I felt bad for all the people that got turned away because they didn‚Äôt ask the right person.

They should‚Äôve also told everyone that The Field of Light doesn‚Äôt turn on until sunset. You can go in anytime after your ticket time until they close. It gets really windy at night, so definitely dress warm and consider scarfs and gloves!

Food/drinks: They currently have one food truck that serves light meals like hot dogs, pizza, hummus, & salad. Price ranging from $7-10. I‚Äôd recommend eating before you get there since there isn‚Äôt much food options in the area. The alcohol station offers beer and wine. We got a bottle of the red blend which was a better deal for 5 people for $38 vs $10 per glass. It had a sweet smokey taste, not bad.

Overall it‚Äôs worth a visit but they are probably still working out the details!<//Review>< pictures>

< review>
(Translated by Google) This is the ‚ÄúField of Light‚Äù by British artist Bruce Munro, which was shown on the slopes of Senorio Gardens in Paso Robles, California, from May 19, 2019 to January 5, 2020.
Visitors can stroll along the path, with a total length of about 1 km. It is an unforgettable artistic experience as the surrounding colors change and change, immersed in art.
Munro has installed ‚ÄúLight of the Wilderness‚Äù in Scotland, Arizona, Denmark, South Korea and Australia.

<rating>5</rating><text>First visit, will have to come back at least 2 more times. Overall score 4.4, but due to unusual circumstance deserved 5 stars.
Let me explain, Covina has some real gems when it comes to Mexican food, and this unassuming shop is one. It is hidden, good luck seeing it from the street. Parking isn't good, COVID tent doesn't help, will be better when restrictions end. (County CDC guidelines are posted very visibly, excellent job there).  It is not an easy location to get to heading north or west. No bathrooms that I saw. Parking, counter, seating are all accessible.
As for the food, outstanding. Do not take a date here as your first stop, when the date is nearly over and you're both hungry cause it went really well and you didn't eat anything cause you were too nervous, then come here for food, trust me your date will love it. If the date didn't go well, drop them off and come here by yourself, at least you will get some good food at a good price. Staff are phenomenal, beyond helpful, if the food wasn't great would still come back at least one more time. Food was prepared quickly and exceeded my expectations. The breakfast burrito was good, as were the asada and carnitas tacos. Breakfast burrito uses fries which are fine, but combo that with the fries for asada fries, you will have something amazing. Tried the chile verde too, was very good, could have used a slightly stronger kick with the chile, but just add some green sauce. The tacos were a little oily, but not in a bad way, breakfast burrito was not oily at all. Beans were good. Will return for a Chile Verde, Colorado, and a Steak Picado burrito in the future. Also need to try the rice. Looking forward to next visit. Highly recommend obviously.<//text>< Resp>
